--- 帖子 #1 ---
I have decided to start a new thread on this topic as I couldn't find another one where my approach fits and I didn't want to cause confusion by posting about my strategy on other people's threads. I posted the below yesterday on Phillip Nel's 5 Min Intraday System (https://www.forexfactory.com/thread/...ntraday-system), hence my reference to Phillip, but then realised he is in the Commercial section, so I'm starting again here under Trading Systems.

==================

I have been a member of FF since 2017, but decided to change my nickname to my real name, so I'm back to being a newbie!

I've been looking for a suitable thread to post my work in and Phillip Nel's work, at least in the earlier pages, is as close as I could find to mine, so it feels right here. But his work is widely respected so I don't really want to get in the way of that. I hope what I post adds value. And as Phillip is a fellow South African, it feels even more like home! Phillip, if you read this, Groete!

I use an 8/21 EMA strategy. There is nothing special about those two numbers. No magic. You could use Phillip's 10/21 EMAs or 10/25 or 6/15, or 12/35, whatever. But I did not suggest 50/200. Smaller MA numbers means the MAs never get very far from price and there is a reason for that - it gives a visual reference for price behaviour, you can judge almost up to the minute how stretched price is from the MAs and whether it is more likely to undergo a correction (reversion to the mean) or to break away from the mean.

This chart summarises my strategy. I wait for a new trend to form, as defined by the EMA crossover, then wait for a pullback to (or close to) the EMAs, which I have now discovered is similar to what Phillip teaches, and then enter a trade. I almost always use stop orders so that if a pullback turns into a reversal, there is less chance of that trade being taken out as price continues the 'wrong' way. Note that I identified a two-bar pullback setup and two inside bar setups. They all represent a pullback, or at least a pause, or a local consolidation period. And after the multi-IB setup, price exploded away. That's just perfect. I look for that kind of setup all the time.

--- 帖子 #7 ---
Here's an interesting example - how do you enter on a fast-moving trend?

This one took off like a rocket. I would be cautious about entering at the end of the breakout bar, or crossover bar, if you like. It's too long and explosive. One of my safety check rules is to avoid such bars (I'll post this safety checklist another time). So the next entry opportunities are the two-bar pullbacks indicated, entering on the tip of the pullback bar. The first one is almost an inside bar setup, but the second bar extends lower than the "mother bar", so it's not. I prefer the second example for an entry because it s a decent pulback and touches the 8 EMA. If that pullback had kept pulling back the buy stop order would likely not have been triggered, firstly, and then we could have followed each pullback bar down (but not too far) until price finally took off again.

--- 帖子 #8 ---
Safety checklist

In my strategy there are no strict rules – you have to understand what is happening on the chart and use the trading tool between your ears. But there are some basics, which I call safety checks. These are things every trader should use for every trade. Basic common sense. I think that if you applied these safety checks properly, you could probably trade ANY system successfully.

1. Dominant trend: Check the trend direction on the next time frame up. I use H4, so I check what is happening on D1. It doesn’t have to be officially up/down yet just as long as it is clearly heading in that direction. It also helps to have a look at what is happening on the next TF down (in my case it’s H1). Sometimes you can see details there that are not clear on your trading TF.

2. S/R obstructions: Avoid trading into support or resistance – this could be horizontal levels or inclined levels as in trend lines or channels. Also, what looks like a strong uptrend on H4 might just be a pullback leg on D1 within a down channel. It would be foolish to buy at the upper boundary line joining successively lower swing high points.

3. Enter when price is close to the EMAs, which means you should avoid entering when there is open space between price and the EMAs. Here the rubber band is stretched, so price is likely to bounce back before it continues with the trend.

4. Avoid long/explosive bars, enter where the bars are short or “quiet” (and such bars are usually close to the EMAs).

5. Avoid trading into price extremes – look at the monthly or weekly chart to see if price is at a long-term low/high.

6. Beware of "old" trends. No trend continues forever, so if a trend has continued for a long time (e.g. it starts in the lower left corner of your screen and goes all the way up to the top right corner) it is an old trend, probably getting tired, its life expectancy is reducing rapidly (as with all of us eventually ). It might continue still, but as a safety precaution, just walk away. Wait for a fresh trend to start.

--- 帖子 #9 ---
Here's a tool to give you a view of trend behaviour across time-frames at "one glance". It comes from a fellow FF member, zoheb01 https://www.forexfactory.com/thread/...dicator-system who produces some very useful One Glance Trader (OGT) tools. It provides a dashboard showing when the three MAs you have selected are all aligned (a green or red block) or grey when they are not aligned fully yet.

The dashboard lets you know when trend (as defined by the three EMAS you have selected) is up, down or neutral across whichever TFs you have selected. It is just one extra tool to help you make decisions about whether to take a trade or not, but if it just clouds your judgement, rather dump it.

Unfortunately the OGT site provides only the closed file (.ex4) not the editable one (.mql4), so the settings it comes with are the default settings and you need to edit them on a chart and save those to a template. Also, as it requires 3 EMAs to work correctly, I use 8/20/21 EMAs and that extra 20 EMA setting has very little effect on the outcome. But you could use a slightly slower set of EMAs, for example 8/21/30 (that's still quick) or 15/30/60 or watever. It's yours to play with.

Attached File(s)   OGT Trend Dashboard v1.2.ex4

--- 帖子 #12 ---
I usually place stops at the recent swing point.

Exits are very important and I haven't cracked that one. At the moment I move to B/E at about 50 pips, depending on which pair it is and I set the target at 100 pips, again depending on the pair. But having said that, I also have a look at chart structure and will adjust the target accordingly. My ideal day (which does happen sometimes!) is when I place about 5 trades, all of them go into profit and I close the whole lot later in the day, even if some of them are not much in profit or even losing. I look at them as a basket of trades and the overall value of the basket for the day.

Yesterday I had that situation and had 2% growth on account balance for the day, then suddenly everything turned around and it evaporated, probably because of the important news events for CAD and USD. I'm still kicking myself over that and it's an area I need to tighten up on. If I get anywhere over 1% for the day and there is something significant coming up in the news I must overcome my instinct to let it run and just take the profit. After all, 1% for the day is still very good!

I did an experiment, as much for myself as anyone else.

I randomly went to CADJPY H4. Note that the chart has plenty of sideways movement, consolidation areas and some fairly jumpy price behaviour. It is not a cherry-picked case. I also zoomed out 1 click to get more on one page.

Using arrows to mark the crossovers I traded EVERY arrow using the methods I normally would. Where I could I traded two legs following one crossover. I used my standard method of using a move to B/E at 50 pips (that saved a number of losses) and a TP of 100 pips. SL was at the previous swing point.

The results are marked on the chart. I placed the label as close to the relevant arrow as I could. The numbers speak for themselves. I doubt we would find this on every chart, but maybe someone here would like to give some of them a go?

--- 帖子 #22 ---
I generally do trade on a Friday but will usually close before the NFPs or if there is any other major news event coming up. I like to close all my trades at the end of the week so that I can have a weekend with nothing nagging at my mind. Sort of a mental health break. I do sometimes leave a trade open by choice, for example if it is already at break-even and the overall look of the trade is good. I have two trades at B/E right now, but as I'm going to be away for a few days next week and off-grid some of the time, I will close everything today.

Regarding this approach being swing trading, I guess you're right as it does take more than a day for many of these trades to work, but I prefer to treat my trades for a day as a basket and look at returns on balance as a whole. If it is around 1% for the day and it's the end of the day I'll close them then.

--- 帖子 #30 ---
The purpose of this thread

I didn't post any rules at the beginning of this thread, trusting in people's decency. So thank you all for respecting each other. I would, however, like to comment on what trading content we post here.

This thread is about using low-number MAs, for example the 8/21 EMAs I use, or similar. It is NOT about using additional indicators. The strategy works as it is and does not need improving. The purpose of this thread is to learn from each other how to get better at using the naked MAs to trade expertly.

So I respectfully ask traders not to introduce indicators or ask for them. If you do use indicators on your charts, please remove them before posting here.

Thank you.

--- 帖子 #31 ---
A note on where to enter a trend

Trends have "legs". When a new trend forms, it goes on its first leg, then after some time, it pulls back significantly. Some traders call such pullbacks a "refresh". Then, most trends experience a second leg. But after that, many trends fade. The odds of a trend continuation after the second leg tend to be lower. Go and have a look at the charts - you will certainly see legs and refreshes.

So I try to enter trades soon after the EMA crossover has taken place, and will do so again at the start of the second leg. But after that, unless it is clear we have a strong trend with good entry points along the way, I will just walk away and look on other charts.

This AUDUSD chart shows two legs and then a refresh / reversal that has two legs down. For me that uptrend ended there and what comes next will be a new trend. You might not agree - in the end it doesn't matter as none of this is very precise - some of the legs and refreshes you will see on the charts look chaotic! We just need to be sure to follow the safety checks I posted previously and to use that trading tool between our ears.

--- 帖子 #36 ---
I have a sell stop order waiting on this USDCAD H4 chart (see chart further down).

My safety checklist:

1. Dominant trend: YES see D1.

2. S/R obstructions: NO.

3. Enter when price is close to the EMAs: YES, but not completely. I waited for price to go back to the EMAs and placed a sell stop order in case price keeps pulling back.

4. Avoid long/explosive bars: YES. The initial crossover bar was a little bit long but the 3 bars that followed are all very short, waiting in a consolidation area. I'm hoping for a breakout from this area.

5. Avoid trading into price extremes: NO, in fact on the monthly, price rejected the upper extreme on the chart and now seems to be moving down

6. Beware of "old" trends: NO (not old).

Entry

I placed a sell stop order at the base of the pullback bar (the second one in the two-bar pullback). This is in case price continues up. I would rather my entry remains un-triggered during that time.

Exit

What I describe here is not necessarily "best practice". I'm not even sure what best practice is . But it seems to work for me. If one of you can help us learn better ways of doing it, please tell us.

My normal practice is to set a 50 pips move-to-breakeven on an EA that sits on my VPS. It's active even when I'm not. That's a safety feature. I have found that by entering close to the crossover point, most trades go at least 50 pips, even if they then go the other way.

Secondly, I usually set a 100 pip target. I have found that this is a large enough target to make decent money. If it is far away it can take a long time to reach it and then stands a greater chance of price reversing and closing at B/E. I prefer to trade mostly intra-day, or just over two days.

My SL is usually just beyond the recent swing point. This means it is sometimes almost the same distance as my 100 pip target, so it's not ideal. Therefore I have adopted an emergency exit procedure to manage this amount of risk.

Emergency exits

If price goes the wrong way after triggering I don't want to lose almost the same as my target is worth, so when it gets to about 50% loss I will partially close about 25% of my trade, then if it keeps going the wrong way I will close another 25% maybe around 2/3 of the "wrong" way. And after that, I throw my hands up and let it go. But ... if price then corrects and goes on with the dominant trend (which it "should" do if I identified the dominant trend correctly), then with the remaining section of the trade I can at least win back what I partially closed.

--- 帖子 #43 ---
Hi josi

As my aim with this thread is for us to develop expertise using naked MAs, I would prefer it if you remove those indicators when you next post, but use them at home, by all means!

My problem (maybe not your problem, and that's ok) with indicators is that we start trusting them / being misled by them (take your pick!), which means we are no longer using our eyes and our mind to the same extent. I have been though this many times before - divert off my path to try greener pastures, get frustrated, and come back to where I feel most comfortable. Ultimately, I am my own holy grail of trading. That's not meant to sound arrogant, just a different perspective on what I should rely on for success.

So for me, I want to stick to just two MAs, nothing else, and this thread is part of that commitment.

To answer your questions, firstly, I've never heard of MMOs before, but my answer would likely be as written above. Then the issue of fakeouts. Could you clarify what you mean by this in our context here? It might mean one thing to you and another to me!

--- 帖子 #44 ---
MMO: you tend to have a first trend move (1-2), then a retracement (2-3), then a second trend move (3-4):

1-2 and 3-4 tend to be of the same/similar length

Fakeout: as you enter with buy stop or sell stop, your trades get filled once an imaginary line is crossed. Oftentimes price tests a new low/high only to return to a range etc. Later on it will move against you: Do you wait for your SL to be hit or do you get out of the trade early once you realize there may not be a follow through?

--- 帖子 #45 ---
On your fakeouts question, if I have correctly identified the dominant trend and followed my safety checks, then I have learned to have faith in the "system". This means that I tend to leave trades to run even if they do go the wrong way because eventually the dominant trend will (should / might ) see them right again. But as my stops tend to be fairly large, I will reduce risk as described earlier by closing 25% of my lot size at about halfway into loss and maybe another 25% after that, depending on what I think is happening. Then, if price does come back I can use what remains of my trade to pull back some profits to cover what I have closed. That's the theory. As I said previously, I don't know if this is best practice (probably not) but it has some clear benefits for me, mainly the psychological one of reducing the fear of losing an entire trade in one big hit.

What do you do in such situations?

--- 帖子 #52 ---
I owe you all an apology. It's that saying "If it's too good to be true, it probably is". And I should have known that when backtesting results show consistently good profits, then something isn't right. I did some more backtesting over the weekend and realised that the Shift -1 setting gives false results. This attempt to predict the future by shifting the signal one bar backwards just does not work, very sadly, if only it did .

This morning I placed three different arrow signals on some 1-minute charts so I could speed up my observations. They all behave differently. Two of them sometimes disappear AFTER the current candle has closed if the EMAs go back up/down on the next candle. So what we see on the charts during backtesting is only those signals that did not disappear, in other words, the ones that worked. The third one seems to behave predictably and dependably, but I still need to watch it a bit more before I make a decision about using it.

So apologies again for misleading you. I should have known better.

This is nearly the exact system I use. A simple  8 & 20 ema cross with the exception of a 200ema to determine trend direction. I then simply wait for engulfing and inside bars early after the crossover. Stop on the other side of the signal bar. TP I generally set for the nearest support or resistance. Aim for a minimum 2:1

Keeps things pretty simple. Good luck to you all!

--- 帖子 #62 ---
Thanks, Szabolcs, I would have posted my trades from today but I was driving a lot and had no time. I placed the trades early this morning and then left them. But I will try to post my trades live.

I received a DM asking about which crossover indicator I am now using. Note that I don't think of this as an "indicator". It is just a visual aid so that I can quickly pick up where the crossovers are while I scan the charts for possible trades.

This is a simple indicator that does only what it is supposed to do. Very importantly, I don't think it repaints. Once the crossover bar has closed, the arrow prints and that's it, it stays there. At least I think so. I spent several hours staring at 1-minute charts yesterday and I didn't see it disappear or shift position once. This is very important for backtesting because you need to see exactly what happened live, otherwise backtesting is misleading.

--- 帖子 #63 ---
Money management is important, as you say. In my case I have simplified it to a 50 pips move to breakeven (B/E) on all trades and a target of between 100 pips and about 130 pips, depending on which pair it is. Some pairs move more in a day than others. So in my case, money management has been reduced to something simple (and perhaps a bit clumsy or not sophisticated, but it works for me).

But more importantly, with just two MAs, you are forced to use your brain and experience. This is not a rule-based, mechanical system. The closest we get to rules here is "guidelines" or "safety checks". And I think that this feature of it is important - weak and stupid as we humans can be, I still think we are better off NOT having fixed rules to follow because we tend to rely on them and over-trust them, and that makes us properly stupid, or at least, that's my experience.

The steps I follow are:

1. Wait for an MA crossover and try to trade the first leg in the trend, or wait for a refresh and try the second leg. I'm not sure about trading more legs than that. Most trends don't get that far, some do, but overall, we will be better off walking away after the second leg unless it's obvious the trend will continue.

2. Wait for price to pull back in some way or other- inside bar, two-bar pullback, outside bar, or a "refresh" - all of these represent either a simple pause or a multi-bar retracement

3. Decide if this is a valid trade by applying the safety checks

4. Place a stop order not too close to where price currently is in case it triggers your trade and then keeps pulling back and back and back.

5. Manage your trade, which means different things to different traders based on your personal style.

I think that's about it.

--- 帖子 #68 ---
Good call josi!

This highlights the saying "I would rather be out of a good trade wishing I was in, than in a bad trade wishing I was out". Preserving capital is almost as important as making it. So it is important to avoid traps like this example. Also, if you are trailing your stop order behind a pullback, don't be in a hurry to get it triggered. It's better to hang back and let price come to you when it finally does resume with the dominant trend. Rather lose a few pips near the beginning than go into loss, perhaps to be stopped out.

Not much. It's probably just the familiarity of forex. I'm familiar with the behaviours of forex pairs and the scale of numbers they have. --- 帖子 #100 ---
Yes, usually I trade the first two legs after the crossover (when a suitable setup arises). After that I am cautious even though that trend might continue, because in most cases trends fade after about two legs, and by then there are almost always better opportunities elsewhere.

So when I responded to your initial question I was focussing just on the bars themselves, not the overall trend structure (was too focussed!). But taking the bigger picture into account I would suggest that this trend has been around for a while, so why tempt fate, unless there are strong signs from higher TFs that it will continue.

I have marked up the main trend on this chart with its leg/refresh structure, but these things are not precise and are not predictable. Just that most trends seem to follow the same basic pattern again and again.

Summarised safety checklist

1. Dominant trend: Not bullish
2. Avoid S/R obstructions:No,there is a resistance level right above the entry
3. Enter when price is close to the EMAs: Partly
4. Avoid long/explosive bars: YES
5. Avoid trading into price extremes: No, not actually, see monthly
6. Beware of "old" trends: Yes,on H4, but ...

--- 帖子 #124 ---
Remember this? That's how it turned out. A refresh on the daily. Check this chart and then scroll down.
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

That's one of the problems we face with trading low number MAs. Minor pullbacks (such as two-bar pullbacks or inside bars) stay more-or-less in line with where price has been moving. But every now and again price retraces well beyond our MAs towards where the 30 or even 60 EMA might be. These will often lead to a stopout and then price resumes with the dominant trend, leaving us stopped out and frustrated. We need to expect these, and knowing that price moves with legs and refreshes really helps because we can (sort of) anticipate them after price has moved steadily for several bars. Also, if price has become extended (moved fast or explosively) then some kind of retracement usually follows. That's how I guessed, successfully this time, that the second refresh might be about to take place.

--- 帖子 #125 ---
One suggestion to solve this problem: use a third MA that emulates the higher TF-MA (in your case D1, I guess). By doing so you can always see (on your trading TF) how price moves relative to the D1-MA.

--- 帖子 #139 ---
This is the sequence that I usually follow when deciding to place a trade. In my case H4 is the trading time-frame and D1 shows the dominant trend.

On the H4 charts:Is there a new trend after a crossover (= first leg) or a second or perhaps even a third leg starting? (This also means to avoid "old" trends unless PA tells you otherwise). Are the recent bars (i) on the "trend side" of the EMAs? (ii) mostly short (iii) fairly close to the EMAs (very little or no open space between bars and EMAs)? Is there any S/R obstruction? I don't mind a consolidation "strip" made up of recent short bars, as long as there is no other S/R level at the same level. If above all OK, look at the monthly and/or weekly chart:Is price approaching an extreme level? If so, make an intelligent (not emotional) decision whether to walk away or proceed If not, proceed. If decision is to proceed, look at the daily:Is the H4 trend aligned with the D1 trend? Is there any S/R obstruction? If still OK, you probably have a trade - look at H1 for more detailed info and a possible better entry than is possible on H4. My advice is always to use a stop order in case price continues pulling back across the EMAs and then into a refresh or reversal, which might stop you out.

Good luck!

--- 帖子 #149 ---
This is not what this thread is about but:

I guess there is no problem at all to trade this on M5 because the range is potentially wide enough.

Al Brooks wrote a book on how to trade ranges - all you need to know is there.

(He wrote another one on reversals, and another one on trends...)

Whether it goes "up for a bit" or not is irrelevant (in my opinion). But a break of structure (in your case resistance area) would, of course, be significant (despite the possibility of a fake-out). A rejection as well, of course....

And - as so often - with your examples, these trades are very interesting because there are opposing ways to analyze them:

a) formally we have a HH and a HL (so an uptrend is feasible)

b) at the same time the last HH was rejected at a zone that was already established as a strong resistance and moved downward from there (therefore this could turn into a downtrend)

--- 帖子 #166 ---
There are 6 H4 bars in a day and 5 days in a trading week, so to put a W1 MA on the H4 chart multiply by 30. EMA 8 becomes EMA 240 and EMA 21 becomes EMA 630. Maybe try the daily MAs first (multiply by 6), at least you'll see them on the H4 chart most of the time!

--- 帖子 #173 ---
Hi,

This is 1 of my trading system & been using it for quite a while. Been taught to follow higher TF trend.  Added EMA100 on H4 chart to validate the buy/sell signals & to act as S/R. The short brown lines are previous week hi/lo (H4) & previous month hi/lo (D1). I used them for TP setting or to lookout for breakout/bounced.

The trading rules are simple:

1) D1 - EMAs crossed for signals + reversal candle patterns, etc

2) H4 - to trigger trades

- D1 EMAs must clearly crossed one another

- EMAs 8 & 20 (H4) crossed

- candle closed below or above EMA100

3) SL & TP - I used H4 previous swing hi/lo or you can set your own.

60-70% of the time, the market will give continuation trade(CT) signals. The remaining 30-40%, the market will be ranging.

GU charts for illustration.CT means continuation trade. Attached Image (click to enlarge)
Attached Image (click to enlarge)
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #176 ---
Yes, a ranging market is always going to be difficult when the system relies on a trend. As a precaution that is why I use stop orders to try to stay clear of price that might go the wrong way, and also I have an EA on a VPS that moves the SL to B/E at 50 pips (sorry for all the acronyms!!). That move to B/E has saved me from losses many times. OK, it also stops me out with no loss when price then goes on to make a profit, but I would "rather be out of a trade wishing I was in, than in a trade wishing I was out".

But the above precautions are just an excuse for not knowing how to stay out of a trending market. That is one of the things I need to get better at. The problem is it's not that easy to see when it's live. Easy afterwards

the basic principles of technical analysis remain the same whatever system, strategy, method you follow.

try to find if entry candle of your method is supported by any other proved, established and easy criteria of technical analysis.

for eg trendlined or flags

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

a) this is the chart you were refering to in your previous posts. after crossover, candle closed below a major trendline (white line..... more than 3 touches)

immediately next caandle closed below a minor trendline (blue... only 2 touches). both suggest a strong downtrend and were excellent entries.

b) even if you missed these there was another flag entry when the trend was well established and in strong momentum.(both emas almost vertically down and pointing south) Attached Image (click to enlarge)

there is so much more than crosses and color change.

--- 帖子 #189 ---
This might just be my bias, but I believe it is generally sound advice to suggest that you try to doing without indicators like RSI, MACD, CCI and so on. And the millions of others like them out there that all seem like greener pastures, but usually (in my experience) turn out to be a disapointment.

What I suggest you do is to look back for trade setups that match your criteria. Then remove RSI and see if it makes any difference at all. I'm prepared to stick my neck out and say that you'll find you could have made the same trades equally confidently if the indicator had not been there. It's like learning to ride a bicycle - at first those fairy wheels seem essential, but they become a hindrance pretty quickly. Let me know how it goes!

--- 帖子 #200 ---
Hi alanh59, I have quoted my recent post where I outlined the sequence I usually follow. That is how I monitor the many charts I have open - one by one at the time of H4 candle closes. It doesn't take long as, in most cases, a quick glance is usually enough to reject most of them. Time is spent on the few that seem to meet the requirements outlined in the sequence. And even then, once I have had a closer look, I reject most of those too.

Where I am (UTC+2) it means my main bit of work is at 8 am, the next candle close is at 12 noon, then 4 pm (this is in my summer - in the southern winter these times shift 1 hour earlier). I am no longer using a Dashboard trend indicator such as the OGT one I posted near the beginning of this thread. The only indicators I use are the MAs, with a quick flip up to the HTFs, mainly the daily, to see how that looks. If the trends on H4 and D1 are aligned, and the safety checks are clear, then there is likely no reason not to pull the trigger.

As I have said previously, the best indicator is your eyes and the best trading tool is the bit between your ears.

--- 帖子 #209 ---
I think I know what you are asking so let me try to answer.

I like to place my SL beyond the recent swing point, but not much more than about 100 pips. If it is more than that I will either walk away from that trade or try to find a minor pullback that will suit my purposes. But my experience tells me that in such cases the trade might be stopped out and then still go back the way I wanted it to. This is why I try to place it beyond the swing point, and also at least 5 pips beyond. If  price gets this far then it usually means that that trade has been invalidated - it wasn't going to work anyway. Here is an example of an SL that looks fairly normal for me.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

3. I think - looking only at H4 - the obvious thing to see was the lower high (of the candles) and the range

All you need is sound money management, losers are part of trading.

--- 帖子 #253 ---
To cut it short: if consecutive candles have countertrend lows or highs, I see that as a sign of weakening momentum

(actually you also take this into account when you use TLs to indicate retracements and the breaks of thereof).

Therefore I wait for a candle which confirms that the bias is still valid. Only then would I consider to trade in that direction.

Add to that the fact that W is still technically up, and I would be extra careful.

--- 帖子 #257 ---
My opinion only:

Once the candle touched the 21EMA and closed green: entry was possible (more risky)

After the candle crossed 8EMA and closed above it: safe entry

If you put a TL along the highs of the retracement candles you will see (I think) that the safe entry more or less represents the TL-break.

That doesn't answer the question what sort of entry you should have chosen: as you can see your entry is pretty late (buy stop). One could also think about a limit buy, if there is a retest level, for example (of course that means that you miss valid trades if there is no retest, on the other hands the ones you do get have a better RR and therefore a higher likelihood of reaching TP). It all depends on your trading style.

--- 帖子 #258 ---
a) consolidation doesn't mean all bearish (or bullish); it just means: price overall moves in a countertrend direction (indicated via TLs)

b) if you looked at it on a much smaller TF, you'd probably see that you had (at least) 2 consolidations both of which could have been entered (for me the question is: does the trend candle break the retracement TL or not? If it does (and all else is in line; i. e. higher TF biases) I'd regard it as a valid trade (you can always have a 2nd or 3rd leg in a retracement but you don't know that beforehand etc).

In short: I am not saying put your entry further away (because that clearly has a negative effect on RR)

Maybe (my opinion only) it is more important that TFs (W, D, H4) have the same trend bias.

[Most important: don't believe anything somebody tells you. Always look at all the pairs you trade and check the last 100 trades. Does someone else's suggestion make sense at all? Does it fit your style of trading? Does it improve your trading habits? Only your own backtesting will tell you if someone else's perspective can be valid for your personal approach.]

--- 帖子 #289 ---
The last few pages in this thread are a rich and exciting resource for all of us who are keen to learn and improve our ability to trade using two crossover MAs. Thank you to all who have contributed .

All of the methods share similar features, basically variations on the same thing. I have tried to summarise them, perhaps too summarised and too simple to be very useful. You will still have to do your own reading.

Identifying a trend

Once the MAs have crossed over and a new trend seems to be forming, all of the methods have ways of confirming that trend. Some use only the trading timeframe (TTF), others also refer up to the higher time frame (HTF):

Methods that use the TTF only include:3 consecutive candles to be beyond both MAs and not touching them - this confirms a new trend is in place a candle that closes beyond the 100 MA acts as trend confirmation (and in practice I suspect this might be close to "3 consecutive candles beyond") MAs that both slope up/down reinforce the confirmation Methods that use the HTF include:HTF MAs that have crossed over in the trend direction, or (less certain) are just visually bullish/bearish, help confirm a TTF trend is in place a previous HTF candle that has closed above/below the MA and is also green/red helps to confirm the TTF trend. Identifying a pullback

Once we have a trend in place, we go to the TTF and look for pullbacks. For convenience and to keep it simple, we can consider small pullbacks, medium pullbacks and long pulbacks:Small pullbacks consist usually of just two or three candles that remain mostly in line with all the other candles in the trend: e.g. pinbar, inside bar, two-bar pullback, engulfing bar Medium pullbacks usually consist of three or more candles that form a local or short-term consolidation area (can be mostly horizontal or inclined as they progress up/down towards the MAs. If inclined, see next bullet) Long pullbacks / retracements / refreshes usually have candles with successively higher/lower highs and lows (not strictly so) and usually retrace into or beyond the MAs. Entries

Once we have a confirmed trend and a pullback we can try to find a suitable entry setup. There are many options depending on the trader's style and I can't cover them all here.Short pullbacks: Inside bar, two-bar pullbacks and engulfing bars are fairly standard - entries just beyond the formation, stops just beyond the other side of the formation are common. But you must vary this according to your preference. Medium pullbacks: If the short-term consolidation is mostly horizontal then if can you place a box around the consolidation, the entry should be just beyond box and the stop either on the other side of the box, or whatever suits you, perhaps the nearest swing point. If you get a candle formation signal (PB, IB EB or other) some will then ignore the box structure and go with that signal. Long pullbacks: In a retracement / refresh you need to be cautious about entering too soon and perhaps being trapped in a losing trade. There are three options I am aware of, all using stop orders:trail the order up/down the retracing candles but conservatively to start with - i.e. keep one closed candle distance away from the current candle. You can tighten this as the retracement progresses and price action (PA) shows that the retracement might be ending wait for a clear PA signal, e.g. an engulfing bar or one of the many other reversal signals wait for a candle to break beyond the trendline (TL) formed by the retracement.  Exits

This is a story all on its own and interestingly, it is not covered much in the material I have been scanning. Perhaps nobody has a clear idea of how to handle this very important aspect of trading.

I haven't captured everything, just the essentials of it, so if your favourite idea isn't here, apologies! All the more reason for us to do the reading and put what we learn into practice. Here's to ever-more successful trading, and please share your trading experiences.

--- 帖子 #290 ---
And that is because EXIT is so difficult and there are numerous methods.

1) S/R from earlier times.

2) ABCD, on a pull back you can se the ABC pattern and then a possible target should be the same length as the AB leg.

3) If you don't have a clue, then set a Risk/Reward. e.g. 1:2.

4) Price Action showing the trend is changing.

5) Lots of indicators shows exits - which we of cause are not using.

6) SL at latest swing.

7) Trailing SL following the structure.

etc. etc.

For me I decide a target from case to case and always a SL at latest swing.

--- 帖子 #293 ---
This supply/demand zone indicator is good for identifying take profit levels.  The zones disappear once they've been taken out, but if you look at where price bounced there was likely a zone there.  You can set it for any timeframe.  0 is for the current timeframe, or you can set it at 60 or 240 (for example) to see 1hr and 4hr zones on a 15 minute chart, etc.  Obviously your trading style will affect what zone to target.  If you like shorter term trades then you can set a TP at the next zone, or if you like swing/position trades then you might want to hold on for more pips.  In that case you can wait for price to bounce off a zone, then break the zone and continue, then use the high/low of the bounce to trail your stop.  Anyway just thought I'd share that.  Have a look and see if it's something you'd like to add to your tool box.  And if not, that's fine too obviously.  Have a good day.

--- 帖子 #300 ---
Based on all of this I have adopted some of the ideas and will explore others. Mainly I have placed the 100 EMA on my charts "officially" (I have been using 100 or 120 on and off for some time). When price closes on the trend side of the 100 EMA I will use this as a signal to trade, if everything else also looks good. And from my backtesting, it usually does all look good.

I also placed the daily EMAs on my H4 chart in dull colours so they don't get in the way. This is so I can keep an eye on the daily EMA status without having to go there each time. But a more useful reason to keep them is because they help show up when the EMAs are horizontal or close together, which is a good time to stay out. It is also an indication that a breakout might be coming. That's what we have currently on this chart - price is in consolidation, with an expected breakout on the way.

--- 帖子 #303 ---
Neither is better, just get used to one and how it behaves, how price relates to it and then stick with it.

It's the same with most of these things - is 8/21 MA better than 9/18 or 10/20 or 12/30 etc?. None of the above. Just learn how one of them behaves, make it an old and predictable friend and then it will be the one for you.

--- 帖子 #305 ---
I have also been working to improve how I trade breakouts. I am doing this by marking up where consolidation zones are and then being careful about where I place my entry and stop. In this case I left the daily EMAs (in dull colours) in place to show how they help highlight where consolidation or sideways movement is taking place.

--- 帖子 #316 ---
It's a difficult one. My exit strategy is to set the SL at the nearest swing point, as long as the risk is not more than about 100 pips, but that varies by currency pair. My app sets the target at 120 pips, currently, and often that's just about right - near a recent high/low, but I will adjust it accordingly.

In this USDCAD example there isn't much to the left on the H4 chart, so you have an arbitrary target to go for. So I would look at the daily chart and there is an opportunity sitting neatly about 150 pips down. Assuming you entered on H4 on the short dotted line, the long dotted line is almost exactly 150 pips down. That's a logical target based on structure. I might reduce that slightly just to be on the safe side.

--- 帖子 #318 ---
I challenge you to remove the Stochastic indicator! Take off those training wheels! But in any event, please remove it when you post.

Another comment - I used to place S/R levels on my charts, much as yours does now, but as I gained experience I realised that all you need is to look left at the level where you plan to place a trade. If it's clear where the trade is headed, then it's clear - place that trade. Certainly, drop a line on the chart and move it up and down a bit to help you see more clearly what you need to see, but you don't need more than that. So my other challenge is for you to remove those S/R lines and take another step towards cleaner charts.

And finally ... can you guess what's coming next?

--- 帖子 #336 ---
An oscillating market will often lead to losses with this system. There are three suggestions I can make:

1. Go down to a lower time frame, then each leg of the oscillation is a big trend

2. Move your stoploss to breakeven early, so you will be stopped out quite often, but it will be soon, so no losses, and sometimes you will get lucky with a good trade.

3. Avoid trading in those market conditions, which is not always easy to identify until after those conditions have happened. That is why I use multiple MAs on my chart because they show more obviously when they are all converging. But I don't like the clutter, so I have set up a separate template for that.

I hope this helps, and can anyone else add to this?

--- 帖子 #364 ---
People - again and again - are spreading the "apparently" obvious rumour that retail traders overall lose (numbers vary from 75-90 per cent):

Up to this day I have not seen one single serious research paper (with more than 1000 participants) that makes such a claim. I believe it is a retail traders' myth that has been spread by marketing people (to keep selling tutoring+products).

The win/loss ratio is, of course, irrelevant to decide whether you are profitable or not: replace it by RR+win-loss-ratio+money management (and you're on your way).

As to your trade: to calculate your RR (already knowing your win-loss-rate from testing) you need to have a TP. If you have a TP, you know what to do (because you know how many of your trades will - statistically speaking - hit your target and how many will fail - and both is part of your trading system, i. e. part of trading).

P.S.: and you did it - news this time may have helped

I think we are at the center of opportunity right now:

--- 帖子 #381 ---
So kind . Here's a thank you gift. Two very useful utilities (for MT4).

They are both scripts, i.e. they don't live on any chart and work just once for each time you activate them. One will change the timeframe across all your charts to match the TF that is on the chart that is open in front of you. Saves a lot of time and effort. The other loads the template you select onto all charts - you need to look at your list of templates and count down to the one you want to load onto all your charts. Remember that number and enter it into the script.

--- 帖子 #387 ---
I don't quite know how helpful this can be (especially including pairs in a range). Did you find any trades using this list?

Wouldn't it be more helpful to look for these two things on higher TF:

a) directional bias: price is in a clear (!) trend

b) price is in a retracement at the moment

For me this means that I should actually be looking/waiting for an entry on my trading TF (the moment the retracement is over).

Anything that may lead directly to a trade is helpful. Anything that doesn't can be disregarded.

Simple answer - as always - most instruments are not clearly trending on higher TFs right now (but either retracing or ranging - especially in ranges: your trend-trading signals very often coincide with a turnaround in ranges).

--- 帖子 #397 ---
Thank you for highlighting this.

Neilpryde's analysis (pullback from the major trend) is not dissimilar. And as you say the MA crossover method is fundamentally a trend-trading system and does not do well in ranging, or sideways conditions and our task with this method is to wait until a clear trend emerges.

--- 帖子 #398 ---
I have tried to capture some of this is a diagram. If I have missed something it would be good if others could add to this using their own chart.

What we are looking for is to enter close to the MA crossover (but waiting for a suitable candle setup) and wait for a clear separation between the EMAs themselves and between the EMAs and price. The ideal (in a bullish case) is for price to 'dance' just above the MA envelope without pulling too far above and without sinking into the envelope.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #399 ---
I have tried to show some conditions we do want for our MA crossover method (except the "explosion" feature shown on the left).

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #400 ---
This to me sounds like an almost magical belief in a crossover.

What does an MA do? It gives you the average price development over a certain period.

If price breaks and closes above this average, chances are somewhat higher that the general evaluation of a fair price has altered for the time being, i. e. buying is an option.

For your "explosive" example that means: MA100 was retested and price closes above it; so the bias is up and it is a valid buy trade. That principle can be apllied to all MAs; no crossover needed.

Just my opinion, of course.

--- 帖子 #401 ---
There's no magic involved, just a different way of looking at the same thing. Some people are visual, others more technical, probably along a continuum. Each to his own, neither is wrong, please allow space for that.

What I am trying to do in a visual kind of way is become more familiar with what the MAs look like when good trading is to be had and what they look like when things are not going well.

--- 帖子 #418 ---
This trade went into profit several times and when came back again and again. So I closed manually for a small profit.

I was expecting price to drop, and if the downward pressure had been stronger it could easily have done that, but after a time I noticed that an 'open space' had developed between the candles and the 21 EMA, as shown on the chart (josi, that's my visual self talking ) which suggests that price will retrace back to the EMAs. That was enough for me to decide to get out. And, of course, the support just below that josi warned of earlier today was in play too. This is why one of my safety checks is to enter as close to the EMAs as possible.

You can see such open spaces all over the place, and very often, a retracement follows.

--- 帖子 #431 ---
As I did last weekend, I am posting a list of currency pairs where the Daily chart (which is the higher time-frame for me) is down or up, not sideways, or bottoming/topping or something else that makes the bias uncertain. To avoid confusion, I am not saying anything about actual trade setups that might appear on H4 (the trading time-frame).

The logic behind this exercise is that the MA crossover method is a trend-following one. It does not perform well in other market conditions, as we have seen over the last two or so weeks. So, if we trade in the direction of the dominant trend, we must surely be increasing our odds of success.

These are the pairs that I think are trending on the daily - I will ignore all the others for the next few days:

GBPAUD down

GBPJPY down

NZDCHF down

NZDJPY down

AUDNZD up

EURGBP up

And that's it. Good trading all.

--- 帖子 #465 ---
Hi vvm, no I don't make notes like this, not in such detail. Mostly my notes are on the charts, like the ones you might have seen recently, e.g. "D1 down".

Usually I follow the same routine (or similar) that I posted earlier in this thread. I will try to find it and post it again. I go to each chart one after the other and look for a crossover, then I check if price is close to the EMAs. If not I leave it. If is is close to the EMAs I look at the daily for a trend, if there is a trend I look more closely and apply the safety checks.

That is the kind of sequence I follow, and it doesn't take long. This is because it's easy to reject those charts that don't qualify, and most of them don't qualify, so the real work is only on a few charts.

--- 帖子 #495 ---
We have all been commenting about how difficult the markets have been in recent weeks, most of us, anyway, even yanah12, who seems otherwise to be doing consistently well. One day we hope to be as good as you, yanah12!

My time away without a signal and no laptop allowed me to think about this without distraction. What is it that made our trading difficult? My simple answer, and I'm sure this is not the only one, came from an exercise I started just before I left, which was to go onto the daily charts, zoom out and look for recent chart patterns. No surprises - most of them are in consolidation. I have now completed that exercise, results below.

This chart compilation is probably too small to see what's going on, but all 16 of these charts (and there are others) show some kind of consolidation pattern - flag, pennant, wedge, range etc and several of these are up against a key S/R level.

The MA crossover method works during trends and poorly in any other conditions. What we need is an early warning system that allows us to stop trading under those conditions before much damage has been done. I am working on that and will post my thoughts another time, but if anyone has comments on this post and tricks to catch consolidation phases quickly, please share them.

--- 帖子 #496 ---
This is exactly the reason why so many people mess their charts up with tons of indicators (so nothing new here).

They want to filter out - what they regard as - noise in order to trade the (clear) moves.

But the more you filter, the more contradicting signals you get.

a)

You won't like to hear this: the best instrument you can use are your eyes (possibly in unison with brain activity).

Scan the area to the left of price and you will (immediately) see what each possible move is up against (where possible consolidation areas are etc).

That won't tell you what will happen (because - depending on the news flow - anything can happen) but it will help you choose the best instrument to trade.

b)

You know that your approach has an edge because you backtested it and evaluated how many trades you will lose on average (statistically speaking); accept that a certain percentage of your trades will go against you and get out of those as early as possible.

c)

Sound money management will take care of the rest.

[Keep in mind that markets are mostly in ranges and that trends are the exception; if you want to trade more often (but why should you?), don't "refine" your working system, but use another system that works for different conditions (one for trending markets, one for ranging markets, one for reversals?).]

--- 帖子 #497 ---
When the emas are flat and the candles are closing above and below both emas is the simplest way to catch consolidation phase quickly.

in fact i love these consolidation phases because usually the pice explodes after such phases in one or the other direction. it is easier to catch such trends and are almost always high probablity and low risk high reward trades.

the descending triangle pattern is the best pattern to trade and i am always on a lookout for it.( CADCHF, NZD JPY, DJ30 on your charts).

wait for a breakout of this pattern, wait for a pullback, and trade the continuation pattern.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

this is what you said in the first post and the chart above is to just remind you your own words.

"This chart summarises my strategy. I wait for a new trend to form, as defined by the EMA crossover, then wait for a pullback to (or close to) the EMAs, which I have now discovered is similar to what Phillip teaches, and then enter a trade. I almost always use stop orders so that if a pullback turns into a reversal, there is less chance of that trade being taken out as price continues the 'wrong' way. "

--- 帖子 #542 ---
I had two good trading days at the end of last week. It’s a relief to be making money instead of struggling not to lose it.

On reflection, one of the reasons seems to be the consolidation zones that I marked out on the charts and avoiding getting caught up in them. My trading was then either breakout trading or, if the consolidation pattern I marked out was clear and large enough, I traded inside the pattern – range trading.

Going forward, this has created a greater awareness of consolidations that I will incorporate into my trading (or my not trading). So while we are range traders, and our MA crossover method depends on trends, we must also embrace consolidations, because we know they often lead to breakouts, as walvekarraje reminded us.

--- 帖子 #587 ---
More than a year ago on another thread I started pointing out that a "pinch" was a profitable setup. Here is one of my early posts about that.

https://www.forexfactory.com/thread/...5#post13835835

I still believe that such setups are worth looking for and waiting for as it seems they lead to high probability trades. In the example below there are multiple crossovers all happening in a tight space. 8/21 EMAs cross over, both of those cross over the 100 EMA and price crosses all three EMAs from bearish to bullish. That setup led to a very nice trend. This seems to happen repeatedly, although not frequently, so be patient and wait for them. You might notice that the chart here is H1. That's because there is less waiting to do.

--- 帖子 #622 ---
Well done - 5.5% in a month is good. But remember that trading with real money is more difficult because there is more psychological pressure. So start with small amounts and get used to experiencing losses of real money.

After a crossover is a good place to look for an entry, as long as the trend is with you. Use the safety checklist I posted earlier in this thread. The important thing is to enter close to the 8 and 21 EMAs and when those two or sometimes all three EMAs are close to each other. As soon as any spaces open up it tells us that price is overbought/sold, or 'stretched' away from the EMAs and almost always you will get a pullback.

This chart (GBPUSD H4) shows a new trend and the places you could enter. Notice that the 100 EMA shows that a strong trend has formed - when the candles and the 8 and 21 EMAs keep a steady distance away from the 100 EMA it suggests that you can enter after many of the pullbacks. But this is a selected, perfect case. Mostly it is not this clear.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #625 ---
This chart shows a typical sequence of events around a reversal. Firstly, note the previous trend slowed down and went into a range, or consolidation. Be sure to mark out that range as soon as you see it forming, e.g. no higher highs is a sign of something going on.

This is easy and obvious after it has happened. Noticing and acting on it is not easy when doing it live.

#1. The 8 and 21 EMAs cross down, but that has happened a lot recently and it is still within the range on the left, so don't act on this, just notice it.

#2. Price breaks below the 100 EMA. This is a sign that the uptrend has ended. You can enter here by placing a sell stop order below the 100 EMA but it is an aggressive style and more risky. A more conservative approach is to wait until all three EMAs are aligned.

#3. The 8 EMA crosses below the 100 EMA, definitely time to get interested, but note that there is a big open space opening up between price and the EMA, so a pullback is very likely - wait for that pullback. The pullback might be a small one, in line with the other candles (e.g. an inside bar or two-bar pullback) or it might be a multi-bar pullback.

#4. The 21 EMA crosses below the 100 EMA, so all we must do is find the best entry point. So we should notice that the pullback has taken place, the EMAs are aligned, price is very close to the 8 and 21 EMAs, even inside the envelope between them, so if there is nothing else getting in the way, like a support level, then place a sell stop order below the 8 EMA. We use a stop order to avoid having the trade triggered and then going the wrong way. The better trends are when price dances down the outside of the 8 EMA (or up in an uptrend), so we wait for price to break out. I have marked a place for the sell stop order at the base of the green bar so that the price level is not near the order at that time. Don't chase price, but wait for it to move outside the EMAs.
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #627 ---
this approach is very similar to one of my systems that I use. I simply go forward based on the signals of the crossover. The change of direction may occur several times a day, but this is included in this strategy.

I have a rule, I don't trade during news. The big advantage of this strategy is that I don't have to predict the prices, I just go with the trend.

no unnecessary stress.

good luck for everyone.

The chart shows the end of a downtrend on the left, then the usual period of confusion / consolidation, followed by an uptrend. On the left I would trade only the red arrows (bearish EMA crossovers) and on the right I would trade only the green arrows. I find the 100 EMA very helpful for being sure about the trend. --- 帖子 #639 ---

--- 帖子 #640 ---
The short answer is that you are right, there haven't been many suitable trades this week that suit an MA crossover, trending market strategy. You could go looking in the lower time frames - what looks like consolidation on the daily might be beautiful big trends on M15.

It does sometimes seem as if the entire forex market goes to sleep, or large parts of it. This might happen before a major economic news release or when there is a major event that could affect world trade. We call this a "risk off" market. https://www.babypips.com/forexpedia/risk-off

Other times the market might be active, just behaving in a way that does not meet the criteria of our particular trading strategy, for example, the MA crossover system we use here is very much a trend trading system, so when markets are ranging, they might still be active, but just not the way we like it. So you could drop to lower TFs as mentioned earlier, or use different strategies that suit what the charts are doing.

Further, I use a more conservative MA crossover approach where I like to include the 100 EMA in my "package" of EMAs. But that slows things down. If you use just two smaller-number EMAs (e.g. 8 and 21), then you will get many more crossovers, but with a lower probability.

My current USD/CHF trade e.g.  was in its third day today, Monday will be 4 days, I still believe in this trade, it currently has a small profit of 4,75 euro but with a swap commission of 1,78 euro ...  it eats away part of your profit, but my TP would largely compensate this. --- 帖子 #673 ---
The overnight swap is relatively minor, so unless it's one of those expensive pairs where the swap is a bit large, just ignore it as one of the costs of doing business. I happen to have two trades open now that are earning a positive overnight swap. Nice feeling to get something for nothing.

The length of time a trade of a certain pip value takes depends on how active the market might be. I have had 100 pip trades open and close in the same day, while at other times they can drag on forever, but that likely means it is in consolidation and it can be very nice if it breaks out. I don't like holding trades for very long because the possibility of surprise news or world events increases for every day the trade is running. The market has been slow recently, so the four days you mentioned is not surprising. I get bored with such trades and will usually close them during Friday.

When you quote the amount a trade has moved, rather do it in pips as we all work with the same pips and so we know what distance of movement you are describing. If my lot size is 1.00, then EUR 4.75 is very little, but for a trade of 0.01 lot size, it is a decent profit.

When you quote the amount a trade has moved, rather do it in pips as we all work with the same pips and so we know what distance of movement you are describing. If my lot size is 1.00, then EUR 4.75 is very little, but for a trade of 0.01 lot size, it is a decent profit.[/quote]

Sorry: this is a rather small trade of 0,08 lot entered at 0,8930 so just 6 pips in profit but targeting 60 pips

--- 帖子 #695 ---
An inside bar pattern shows indecision. I like to call it a mini-consolidation. So if you treat it like any consolidation by trying not to get caught up in it but sitting waiting for a breakout in the direction of the dominant trend you won't go far wrong.

a) you can do what you want

b) the trade may work out for you as anything can happen

c) FOMO tends to have disastrous consequences

d) for a trend reversal (from down to up) trade I would look for 2 things:

1. a higher high (which means a clear break of structure)

2. a higher low

as far as I can see we have neither on your chart (+ price is below MA)

--- 帖子 #703 ---
Moving averages was in my early days always on my charts. In the last years i can do it without it, means not they can not help!

I will put some thoughts here using moving averages.

First as here shared do not clutter the chart with countless averages. Two will for sure enough. Now look what you will trade, what is your focus? Will you trade the high timeframes H4 and above? Will you trade fast the M1? What pair you wil trade? Watch for settings that suit the pair, what has the moving averages done in the past?

Moving averages work good if they first move! Many new trader out have trouble using it wise, want pick up the cross and let not doing first the move. So the result is, they search for the golden setting over and over again or cut using it at all. Waiting is the hard point and sometimes it must be learned.

Now to a example. If we can wait for consolidation first, we can also wait for a move. If we done this part good, we have the strength to wait for correction and wait further for the entry. All these waiting, huuh ...

It was M1 and the averages i use here are the SMA 20 & 60

--- 帖子 #714 ---
To put it simply:

the difference is that in the case of "wishful thinking" you do not have a real, physical signal on the chart,

whereas in analysis you do (and act only after this was established).

As I wrote: the secure (non-gambling) way to consider is:

a) wait for a higher high (break of structure)

b) wait for a higher low (and enter after this was established)

[buy low vs sell high]

--- 帖子 #719 ---
To continue with the USDCHF possible reversal discussion, I think it's helpful to distinguish between signs and signals (my own ramblings again, might not be the official way these words are used).

Signs, the way I see it, are ways we get a sense that something is going on, a market shift might be happening, a pair might be bottoming out, perhaps to reverse, and so on. But these are far from being signals. Signals are specific and more objective and tell is that we can go ahead and enter a trade, or be ready to enter soon.

Based on this, I don't believe there are any signals that this pair is about to reverse. But I do see signs that a reversal might be brewing. I went looking for such signs; there are not many, TBH.

I have posted all of these four charts below:

The monthly shows price at an all-time low, bottoming out. This started perhaps about 13 years ago (so we shouldn't hold our breath for the breakout!). But it might mean that the odds are more in favour of a move up than a move down. Unless it moves down from here . In fact, as the three EMAs are now close to each other, it shows consolidation. Another sign is that price has been pushing up against the 100 EMA. For me this is often a sign of a trend weakening, perhaps to reverse. The only action from all of this is to be cautious about selling, but as the scale of the monthly chart is vastly different from that of H4, perhaps it is meaningless for practical daily trading purposes.

The weekly chart seems to be a bit stretched down, perhaps due for a correction, again a possible caution about going short. But it's still very much bearish.

The daily does show a failure to break below the previous low, but otherwise it's clearly bearish.

H4 is interesting. It looks like it has entered a local range, and might stay between those levels a bit longer. But if it is going with the existing momentum, then it's also still bearish until we learn otherwise.

So to conclude this long story, there are signs, weak ones, that a reversal might take place in the future, but no signals to go long whatsoever. To go long josi commented that he will wait for a higher high and a higher low. My approach is to wait until the 8 and 21 EMAs and the price bars have all crossed to the other side of the 100 EMA, and then also to apply my safety checks. In the end these two approaches probably end up being much the same thing.

--- 帖子 #732 ---
yanah12 can correct me if I am wrong, but he has a (very) slightly different approach to me that he came with when I started this thread and it is very successful. He uses the 8 and 20 EMAs and monitors the daily chart for an EMA crossover. When he gets a crossover signal, he drops to H4 for a trigger. He is not very concerned about waiting for a pullback as I am. This is copied from one of his posts:

The trading rules are simple:
1) D1 - EMAs crossed for signals
2) H4 - to trigger trades
- D1 EMAs must clearly crossed one another
- EMAs 8 & 20 (H4) crossed
- candle closed below or above EMA100
Previous day candle needs to close below (sell) or above (buy) 8 EMA. To sell. previous day candle must be a bearish candle & vice versa.

I hope this helps?

It is important that "the force is with you", which means you need to check that the dominant trend (on the next higher TF) is clearly in your favour.

--- 帖子 #759 ---
I can't reply for yanah12, but in my opinion there is no rule for how many trades to run at the same time. It depends on how experienced you are and what you feel comfortable managing. Probably a maximum of 6 at once is about right. Some people do advise trading one pair only, e.g. EURUSD and get to know it so well that you become good at trading it. I have heard others say "If it moves I'll trade it", but that is reckless, I think, because there are thousands of instruments out there and you can't hope to master the behaviour of all of them (e.g forex, indices, shares etc have different characteristics).

If your system identifies a small number of trades you can have many charts open hoping to get at least one or two signals a day. If your system produces lots of signals, then you need to be careful and choose the better ones, always limiting yourself to how many trades you are able to manage properly, also not to overload your account. Hope this helps.

--- 帖子 #761 ---
If I may ask; where is the best place to place a stop loss...

Regards,

--- 帖子 #762 ---
There's no "best" place, rather choices you need to make. Personally, I like to place my SLs beyond the most recent swing point, but that makes for quite large SL distances and risk-reward ratios close to 1. Others prefer tighter stops, for example, if you have a pinbar or an inside bar or two-bar pullback setup then they might place the stop just beyond that setup - the other end of the PB or just beyond the mother bar, etc. That gives you a much better risk-reward ratio, eg 25 pips loss, 100 pips profit = RR of 4. But then you stand a greater risk of being stopped out because the SL is close.

--- 帖子 #780 ---
I have 26 forex charts open all the time (made up of the majors and minors but no weird ones, I also avoid EURNZD and GBPNZD). Then I scan them for setups. Once you have settled on a trading system, it's usually quick to pick up suitable setups - mostly it's a matter of rejecting charts that are not suitable, then spending time looking at those that might be suitable, mostly rejecting those too, and finally identifying one or two that seem just right. I have set up some simple indicator dashboards that pick up those that meet my conditions, eg where both H4 and D1 have EMAs crossed in the same direction (yanah12's method). That does make things more obvious, but I'm not sure it's any quicker, and by scanning all of them manually I get a better feel for overall trends or market behaviour, or even possible setups I might have missed using just a dumb indicator dashboard.

Correlations are a bit of a mystery to me. I just note that sometimes the entire market seems to have slowed down (risk off) or it's active across the board. I try not to trade more than two directly related pairs at the same time e.g. NZDxxx or GBPxxx pairs.

--- 帖子 #783 ---
I hear you Alistair about EJ playing jokes. But this was a good trade from the crossover that I refer to on this chart.

For good reasons we are all looking for support and resistance levels because we know how valuable they are to us as traders. One thing that I make note of are " master candles ". If there are at least 3 bars that are engulfed by the master candle then that is something to take notice of. I treat the master candles simply as support and resistance levels. Therefore there are bounces..fakeouts..breakouts / pullbacks / continuation...etc..etc.

You see that the highs of the 2 last 4 hr candles have bounced right off of the master candle low. ( I have at 5/02..16:00 ). Also notice that the last crossover

( I have it at 5/15 ..20:00 ) was one of six candles that were contained within the master candle. You can look at the master candle as a 'congestion' phase. Congestions usually lead to an impulse ( sometimes fakes...sometimes real ).  Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #801 ---
We look to the higher time frame (HTF) in order to decide which way price is likely to move. Recently I have been thinking about what the qualities or conditions are that would give us the best HTF opportunities. This is what I have come up with.

1. The EMAs are nicely separated, but not 'ballooning' apart, best is if they are parallel.

2. The price bars are 'dancing' along the outside of the EMAs - not crossing into the space between them and not pulling away from them.

As always, this is easy afterwards, but less easy when doing it live.
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

hello. has anyone made an EA based on this strategy? is it possible to automate its process or some times its based on trader decision?

--- 帖子 #816 ---
It's worth a try if you are willing to do that.

My brief would be as follows:

1. Trading TF AND HTF EMAs (e.g. 8 and 21 EMA) to be aligned (both up / both down). Another option we could test is to have 3 EMAS (e.g 8/21/55 or 8/21/100) all aligned on each TF, but we can test that later?

2. Place a trade at the close of a candle that opens inside the fast EMA and then closes outside of it (i.e. in the direction of the trend)

3. TP at a set number of pips (to make it easier for you - we can change it later to another system)

4. Move to B/E at a set number of pips.

5. I'm not sure about the SL, perhaps for now make it a set number of pips.

How does that sound? I have done some backtesting and overall it does seem to be a winner. It will be interesting to see on the strategy tester how it does.

--- 帖子 #820 ---
First trade of the week.

I entered at the top of a minor consolidation, which is where breakouts often occur. It's like flyfishing - place your fly where trout often lurk, waiting for food!

But what I want to point out is the tight formation just below, where all three EMAs have come close together - I call this a "pinch". But it's really just a consolidation, and the EMAs go sideways, naturally. It seems whenever we get a pinch, then a decent trend forms afterward. And if you miss the initial breakout, there is almost always a pullback and that seems to be a good place to enter.
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Here is another currency pair with a similar sideways consolidation and lovely trend breakout. It's a common feature - go looking and you'll see this all over the place. You can trade the initial breakout from consolidation (but doing it live means you don't always know which way it will break), or you can wait for the pullback, by which time the direction is clear.
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #838 ---
Hi Uru-trader, if you haven't used an EA before, I suggest you look around on the internet and learn about using an EA, the benefits and drawbacks (beware of the drawbacks!). There are plenty of videos showing how to install one. A trick - once you have placed the EA in the experts folder you do not need to close down your MT4 platform and reboot it. Simply go to Navigator in MT4, right-click on Experts and choose refresh. The EA should then appear in that section.

--- 帖子 #841 ---
It makes no difference which TF you open it on - click the down arrow in the inputs window and select what you want. The timeframe options control which three TFs you want the EMAs to be active on, i.e. all aligned UP or DOWN. The EMA option is where you selected which EMAs you want to be working with on your three TFs, eg 8/21/100.

--- 帖子 #843 ---

--- 帖子 #844 ---
The first item in each section is a trigger. If you read my requirements the trigger is described there. So the Trigger EMA might be the 8 EMA (that's what I was asking for, but it's an option) and the Trigger TF is where that crossover will take place. The default is 5M. So in that case a 5-minute candle must open one side of the 8 EMA and close the other side of the 8 EMA. So if all three EMAs are aligned on all three of your TFs, then as soon as the trigger process happens, it will place a trade.

So far it is working well for me, but on small lots. I might increase to 0.02 in the next few days and more later, hoping it continues working well. The danger is that just as one gains confidence in an EA, conditions change and it makes a mess.

--- 帖子 #864 ---
I'm slowly working out some of the behaviour of eurusd-thijs's EA.

When I started using it it seemed that the M5 candle produced too many trades (but maybe not, I haven't used it enough to be sure) and so I tried M30, H1 and even H4 as the trigger candle. Remember that the trigger candle is the one that must open on the 'wrong' side of the fast EMA, and close on the trend side of it.

I originally wanted H4 because that is my trading TF and I know that when a bar starts one side of the EMAs and closes outside of them (on the trend side), it is often a good place to enter. But H4 is not a good idea because H4 candles can be too long, as in this example. The EA followed the rules perfectly, but the candle is very long (98 pips) and price is far away from the mean, so of course there is going to be a pullback. But using H4 does reduce the number of trades. So somewhere between M5 and H4 is probably right, the sweet spot. For now I'm thinking it is M30.

Another option is to set a limit to how long the trigger candle can be, eg 0.5 of ATR. In this example, ATR is about 55 pips, so 0.5 of that would mean any candle that is more than about 27 pips would be ignored as a trigger. Then we could use any TF for the trigger candle, which might be an improvement for the EA.
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #934 ---
Both yen pairs that were aligned earlier today have gone out of alignment. That's why I set them to sell only - it was clear they were stretched and would likely correct. Others that were suitable yesterday have also gone out of alignment.

It seems the markets do this - for a few days most pairs are working well and all of a sudden the whole lot go off the boil. No surprise, because it's Big Money that moves the markets and if something is troubling them it will trouble most of them and so we get "risk off" sentiment. So if we catch the move to risk off at the wrong time, most of the trades we place that morning might end up going wrong. But our 3x3 system also then will quickly stop working as the lowest TF stops being aligned.

So while we need to manage the EA and stop it from trading overbought/sold pairs, or pairs at an extreme level, or pairs that are sitting at S/R key levels, or pairs that are in old trends that must inevitably come to an end sooner rather than later, we can't get that right all the time.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

EDIT: And a few hours later there is just one pair (of 28) that meets the 3x3 criteria. Something is happening in the forex market, either a pullback all round or the beginnings of a reversal in many of the pairs, if I have understood things correctly.

I've been monitoring this thread for a long while now. I reminded me of how I used to trade as well. 8-21ema with trendline breaks and retests, SR breaks and retest, fibs and drilling down to a lower timeframe. I've done with scalping (15m-1m) and with swing trading.

--- 帖子 #941 ---
Take note: I haven't backtested this thoroughly so I don't have stats for this. I'm just hoping to join in the ride here. I will utilise a very old but basic entry method from a guy called Hector Deville from his 3SMA course. I will incorporate some ICT techniques as an alternative method of technical analysis. However, I will try to keep it simple.

Trading PlanWatchlistScan forex pairs, metals, commodities, energy CFDs over weekend Choose those which look good and build a watchlist for the coming week Use push alerts to get notified of potential opportunities and also to step away from charts  TimeframesW1/D1 for overall trend and macrostructure H4 for mini/inner trend and microstructure H4/H1/M15/M5 for entry  Trend Condition8-21 EMAs crossover Sloping and parallel EMAs  Entry ModelHorizontal/Trendline Breakout (Hector Deville Method)Breakout-Pullback-Continuation (BPC) Breakout-Pullback-Retest (BPR)  Micro Market Structure Shift (MSS)Fair Value Gap (FVG) entry   ConfluenceFibonacci Levels Fibonacci Extensions (Targets) Support Resistance Imbalances / FVG  Important Levels (Possible Trend Reversal)Monthly High/Lows Weekly High Lows Significant S/R  Stop-LossBehind candle Behind FVG Behind Swing  Take-Profit138.2% extension 161.8% extension Monthly High/Lows Weekly High/Lows Trailing SL behind EMAs (current or lower TF)  CorrelationDo not open positions on correlated charts  Ok, I think i've detailed my trading plan out enough. I will post screenshots and images of the entry methods in further posts.
